**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Task: Generate Javadoc for Kafka Record Batch Serialization

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kafka--e678b4b (mirror of apache/kafka)
**Output:** Write your summary to `/workspace/documentation.md`; edit source files directly

## Objective

Generate Javadoc comments for Kafka's record batch serialization classes in `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/`. These classes handle the binary encoding of Kafka message batches and are critical for correctness and performance.

## Scope

Document the following classes:
- `RecordBatch` — interface defining a batch of records
- `DefaultRecordBatch` — concrete implementation of a magic v2 batch
- `MemoryRecords` — in-memory collection of record batches

For each class, document:
- Class-level Javadoc: purpose, role in the Kafka protocol, thread-safety guarantee
- Key public methods: `@param`, `@return`, `@throws` tags
- Performance characteristics where relevant (e.g., lazy decoding, copy-on-write)
- Cross-references using `{@link}` to related classes

## Quality Bar

- Thread-safety must be explicitly stated for every class (thread-safe, not thread-safe, or conditionally thread-safe)
- Performance implications must be noted for serialization/deserialization methods
- Do not add Javadoc to private methods
- Use standard Javadoc tags: `@param`, `@return`, `@throws`, `@see`, `{@link}`

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not change implementation logic
- Do not document internal/private fields

---

## What was documented

### `RecordBatch.java` — interface

- **Class Javadoc** expanded from 4 lines to a full description covering: the three magic version epochs (v0/v1/v2) and their semantics, how instances are obtained via `Records.batches()`, explicit **not thread-safe** statement, and `@see` cross-references.
- **Method enhancements:** `ensureValid()` gained `@throws CorruptRecordException`; `hasProducerId()` gained a proper `@return`; `streamingIterator()` gained a **Performance note** on lazy decompression and buffer-pool reuse; `offsetOfMaxTimestamp()` gained numbered edge-case notes and a **Performance note** on full-scan cost.

### `DefaultRecordBatch.java` — concrete implementation

- **Class Javadoc** kept the existing wire-format schema and compaction semantics, and added an explicit **not thread-safe** statement calling out the in-place mutation methods.
- **New method Javadocs** for all previously undocumented public methods: `baseTimestamp()`, `recordInputStream()`, `writeEmptyHeader()` (12 params), `writeHeader()` (17 params, `@throws`), `sizeInBytes(long, Iterable<Record>)`, `sizeInBytes(Iterable<SimpleRecord>)`, `incrementSequence()`, `decrementSequence()`.

### `MemoryRecords.java` — in-memory records collection

- **Class Javadoc** expanded to cover purpose, a bullet-list of **performance characteristics** (O(1) header access, lazy decompression, cached `validBytes()`, zero-copy `buffer()`/`slice()`), explicit **not thread-safe** statement, and `@see` cross-references.
- **New method Javadocs** for all public methods that lacked them: all `builder()` overloads (9 variants), all `withRecords()` / `withIdempotentRecords()` / `withTransactionalReco
... (truncated)

The schema is given below:\\n47:  *\\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\\n50:  *  Length => Int32\\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\\n63:  *\\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\\n66:  *\\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\\n72:  *\\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\\n81:  *\\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\\n86:  *\\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\\n91:  *\\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\\n98:  *\\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n102:  */\\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends The schema is given below:\n47:  *\n48:  * RecordBatch =>\n49:  *  BaseOffset => Int64\n50:  *  Length => Int32\n51:  *  PartitionLeaderEpoch => Int32\n52:  *  Magic => Int8\n53:  *  CRC => Uint32\n54:  *  Attributes => Int16\n55:  *  LastOffsetDelta => Int32 // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n56:  *  BaseTimestamp => Int64\n57:  *  MaxTimestamp => Int64\n58:  *  ProducerId => Int64\n59:  *  ProducerEpoch => Int16\n60:  *  BaseSequence => Int32\n61:  *  RecordsCount => Int32\n62:  *  Records => [Record]\n63:  *\n64:  * Note that when compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n65:  * directly following the count of the number of records.\n66:  *\n67:  * The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that follow the CRC). It is\n68:  * located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the magic byte before deciding how to interpret\n69:  * the bytes between the batch length and the magic byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC\n70:  * computation to avoid the need to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by\n71:  * the broker. The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n72:  *\n73:  * On Compaction: Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first and last offset/sequence\n74:  * numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is required in order to be able to restore the\n75:  * producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did not retain the last sequence number, then following\n76:  * a partition leader failure, once the new leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence\n77:  * expected number would no longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an\n78:  * unexpected OutOfOrderSequence error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be preserved for\n79:  * duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by verifying that the first and\n80:  * last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that producer.\n81:  *\n82:  * Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may still retain an empty\n83:  * batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as described above. These empty batches\n84:  * are retained only until either a new sequence number is written by the corresponding producer or the producerId\n85:  * is expired from lack of activity.\n86:  *\n87:  * There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction. The BaseTimestamp\n88:  * field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the\n89:  * BaseTimestamp will be set to -1 (NO_TIMESTAMP). If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the BaseTimestamp\n90:  * will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction markers in the batch should be removed.\n91:  *\n92:  * Similarly, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current records if the timestamp type\n93:  * is CREATE_TIME. For LOG_APPEND_TIME, on the other hand, the MaxTimestamp field reflects the timestamp set\n94:  * by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the MaxTimestamp of an empty batch always retains\n95:  * the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n96:  *\n97:  * The current attributes are given below:\n98:  *\n99:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n100:  *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n101:  *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n102:  */\n103: public class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch // Note that this differs from produce up-conversion where the timestamp type topic config is used and the log append\\n270:         // time is generated if the config is LOG_APPEND_TIME. Otherwise, the producer\\n291:             // could incorrectly see an out of sequence error.\\n292:             builder.overrideLastOffset(originalBatch.lastOffset());\\n293: \\n294:         return builder;\\n295:     }\\n296: \\n297:     /**\\n298:      * Get the byte buffer that backs this instance for reading.\\n299:      */\\n300:     public ByteBuffer buffer() {\\n301:         return buffer.duplicate();\\n302:     }\\n303: \\n304:     @Override\\n305:     public MemoryRecords slice(int position, int size) {\\n306:         if (position < 0)\\n307:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid position: \\\" + position + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n308:         if (position > buffer.limit())\\n309:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Slice from position \\\" + position + \\\" exceeds end position of \\\" + this);\\n310:         if (size < 0)\\n311:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Invalid size: \\\" + size + \\\" in read from \\\" + this);\\n312: \\n313:         int availableBytes = Math.min(size, buffer.limit() - position);\\n314:         // As of now, clients module support Java11 hence can't use ByteBuffer::slice(position, size) method.\\n315:         // So we need to create a duplicate buffer and set the position and limit. Duplicate buffer\\n316:         // is backed by original bytes hence not the content but only the relative position and limit\\n317:         // are changed in the duplicate buffer. Once the position and limit are set, we can call the\\n318:         // slice method to get the sliced buffer, which is a backed by the original buffer with the\\n319:         // position reset to 0 and limit set to the size of the slice.\\n320:         ByteBuffer slicedBuffer = buffer.duplicate();\\n321:         slicedBuffer.position(position);\\n322:         slicedBuffer.limit(position + availableBytes);\\n323:         // Reset the position to 0 so that the sliced view has a relative position.\\n324:         slicedBuffer = slicedBuffer.slice();\\n325: \\n326:         return readableRecords(slicedBuffer);\\n327:     }\\n328: \\n329:     @Override\\n330:     public Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches() {\\n331:         return batches;\\n332:     }\\n333: \\n334:     @Override\\n335:     public String toString() {\\n336:         return \\\"MemoryRecords(size=\\\" + sizeInBytes() +\\n337:                 \\\", buffer=\\\" + buffer +\\n338:                 \\\")\\\";\\n339:     }\\n340: \\n341:     @Override\\n342:     public boolean equals(Object o) {\\n343:         if (this == o)\\n344:             return true;\\n345:         if (o == null ||                                             ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream,\n266:                                                                  final long deleteHorizonMs) {\n267: It is the fundamental unit of data transfer between producers,\n * brokers, and consumers.\n *\n * <p>The batch format has evolved over three major versions, identified by the {@link #magic()} byte:\n * <ul>\n *   <li><b>Magic v0</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V0}): Legacy format. A batch always contains exactly\n *       one record when uncompressed; multiple records are allowed only under compression.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v1</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V1}): Adds per-record timestamps. Batches generally\n *       contain multiple records regardless of compression. Adds idempotent producer support\n *       (producer id, epoch, sequence numbers) and transactional semantics.</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * <p>Instances of this interface are obtained by iterating over a {@link Records} object (e.g.\n * {@link MemoryRecords} or {@code FileRecords}) via {@link Records#batches()}. This class provides both read and\n * in-place-mutation access to a single batch encoded in the Kafka binary wire format. The on-wire\n * schema is:\n *\n * <pre>\n * RecordBatch =&gt;\n *   BaseOffset            =&gt; Int64\n *   Length                =&gt; Int32\n *   PartitionLeaderEpoch  =&gt; Int32\n *   Magic                 =&gt; Int8\n *   CRC                   =&gt; Uint32\n *   Attributes            =&gt; Int16\n *   LastOffsetDelta       =&gt; Int32  // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n *   BaseTimestamp         =&gt; Int64\n *   MaxTimestamp          =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerId            =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerEpoch         =&gt; Int16\n *   BaseSequence          =&gt; Int32\n *   RecordsCount          =&gt; Int32\n *   Records               =&gt; [Record]\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p>When compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n * directly following the count of the number of records.\n *\n * <p>The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that\n * follow the CRC). It is located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the\n * magic byte before deciding how to interpret the bytes between the batch length and the magic\n * byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC computation to avoid the need\n * to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by the broker.\n * The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction:</b> Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first\n * and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is\n * required in order to be able to restore the producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did\n * not retain the last sequence number, then following a partition leader failure, once the new\n * leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence expected number would no\n * longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an unexpected\n * {@code OutOfOrderSequence} error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be\n * preserved for duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by\n * verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that\n * producer.\n *\n * <p>Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may\n * still retain an empty batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as\n * described above. These empty batches are retained only until either a new sequence number is\n * written by the corresponding producer or the producerId is expired from lack of activity.\n *\n * <p>There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction.\n * The {@code BaseTimestamp} field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the\n * batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to\n * {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP}. If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the\n * {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction\n * markers in the batch should be removed.\n *\n * <p>Similarly, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current\n * records if the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME}. For\n * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, on the other hand, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field\n * reflects the timestamp set by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the\n * {@code MaxTimestamp} of an empty batch always retains the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n *\n * <p>The current attributes bit layout:\n * <pre>\n *  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n *  -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> This class is <em>not</em> thread-safe. The underlying\n * {@link ByteBuffer} is accessed without synchronisation. Concurrent reads or any combination of\n * reads and in-place mutations (e.g. {@link #setLastOffset}, {@link #setMaxTimestamp},\n * {@link #setPartitionLeaderEpoch}) from multiple threads requires external synchronisation.\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch {\n    static final int BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET = 0;\n    static final int BASE_OFFSET_LENGTH = 8;\n    static final int LENGTH_OFFSET = BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET + BASE_OFFSET_LENGTH;\n    static final int LENGTH_LENGTH = 4;\n    static final int PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET = LENGTH_OFFSET + LENGTH_LENGTH;\n    static final int PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_LENGTH = 4;\n    static final int MAGIC_OFFSET = PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET + PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_LENGTH;\n    static final int MAGIC_LENGTH = 1;\n    public static final int CRC_OFFSET = MAGIC_OFFSET + MAGIC_LENGTH;\n    static final int CRC_LENGTH = 4;\n    static final int ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET = CRC_OFFSET + CRC_LENGTH;\n    static final int ATTRIBUTE_LENGTH = 2;\n    public static final int LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_OFFSET = ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET + ATTRIBUTE_LENGTH;\n    static final int LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_LENGTH = 4;\n    static final int BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET = LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_OFFSET + LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_LENGTH;\n    static final int BASE_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH = 8;\n    static final int MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET = BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET + BASE_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH;\n    static final int MAX_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH = 8;\n    static final int PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET = MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET + MAX_TIMESTAMP_LENGTH;\n    static final int PRODUCER_ID_LENGTH = 8;\n    static final int PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET = PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET + PRODUCER_ID_LENGTH;\n    static final int PRODUCER_EPOCH_LENGTH = 2;\n    static final int BASE_SEQUENCE_OFFSET = PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET + PRODUCER_EPOCH_LENGTH;\n    static final int BASE_SEQUENCE_LENGTH = 4;\n    public static final int RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET = BASE_SEQUENCE_OFFSET + BASE_SEQUENCE_LENGTH;\n    static final int RECORDS_COUNT_LENGTH = 4;\n    static final int RECORDS_OFFSET = RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET + RECORDS_COUNT_LENGTH;\n    public static final int RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD = RECORDS_OFFSET;\n\n    private static final byte COMPRESSION_CODEC_MASK = 0x07;\n    private static final byte TRANSACTIONAL_FLAG_MASK = 0x10;\n    private static final int CONTROL_FLAG_MASK = 0x20;\n    private static final byte DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK = 0x40;\n    private static final byte TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK = 0x08;\n\n    private final ByteBuffer buffer;\n\n    DefaultRecordBatch(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        this.buffer = buffer;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public byte magic() {\n        return buffer.get(MAGIC_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void ensureValid() {\n        if (sizeInBytes() < RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD)\n            throw new CorruptRecordException(\"Record batch is corrupt (the size \" + sizeInBytes() +\n                    \" is smaller than the minimum allowed overhead \" + RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD + \")\");\n\n        if (!isValid())\n            throw new CorruptRecordException(\"Record is corrupt (stored crc = \" + checksum()\n                    + \", computed crc = \" + computeChecksum() + \")\");\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Gets the base timestamp of the batch, which is used to calculate each individual record's\n     * absolute timestamp from its delta value encoded in the record.\n     *\n     * <p>For batches where the delete horizon flag is set, the base timestamp is overloaded to\n     * store the delete horizon instead. Use {@link #deleteHorizonMs()} to access that value safely.\n     *\n     * @return The base timestamp in milliseconds since the Unix epoch\n     * @see #deleteHorizonMs()\n     */\n    public long baseTimestamp() {\n        return buffer.getLong(BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long maxTimestamp() {\n        return buffer.getLong(MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public TimestampType timestampType() {\n        return (attributes() & TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK) == 0 ? TimestampType.CREATE_TIME : TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long baseOffset() {\n        return buffer.getLong(BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long lastOffset() {\n        return baseOffset() + lastOffsetDelta();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long producerId() {\n        return buffer.getLong(PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public short producerEpoch() {\n        return buffer.getShort(PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int baseSequence() {\n        return buffer.getInt(BASE_SEQUENCE_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    private int lastOffsetDelta() {\n        return buffer.getInt(LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int lastSequence() {\n        int baseSequence = baseSequence();\n        if (baseSequence == RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE)\n            return RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE;\n        return incrementSequence(baseSequence, lastOffsetDelta());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CompressionType compressionType() {\n        return CompressionType.forId(attributes() & COMPRESSION_CODEC_MASK);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int sizeInBytes() {\n        return LOG_OVERHEAD + buffer.getInt(LENGTH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    private int count() {\n        return buffer.getInt(RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Integer countOrNull() {\n        return count();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void writeTo(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        buffer.put(this.buffer.duplicate());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void writeTo(ByteBufferOutputStream outputStream) {\n        outputStream.write(this.buffer.duplicate());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean isTransactional() {\n        return (attributes() & TRANSACTIONAL_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    private boolean hasDeleteHorizonMs() {\n        return (attributes() & DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public OptionalLong deleteHorizonMs() {\n        if (hasDeleteHorizonMs())\n            return OptionalLong.of(buffer.getLong(BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET));\n        else\n            return OptionalLong.empty();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean isControlBatch() {\n        return (attributes() & CONTROL_FLAG_MASK) > 0;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int partitionLeaderEpoch() {\n        return buffer.getInt(PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Returns an {@link InputStream} that reads the raw (possibly compressed) record bytes of this\n     * batch, starting immediately after the fixed batch header.\n     *\n     * <p>If compression is enabled, the stream transparently wraps the underlying buffer bytes with\n     * the appropriate decompression codec, using buffers obtained from the supplied\n     * {@link BufferSupplier} to reduce allocations.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> The returned stream holds a reference to a buffer obtained from\n     * {@code bufferSupplier}. Callers must close the stream after use to release that buffer back\n     * to the supplier pool.\n     *\n     * @param bufferSupplier supplier of temporary decompression buffers; must not be {@code null}\n     * @return an {@link InputStream} over the (possibly decompressed) record bytes\n     */\n    public InputStream recordInputStream(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        final ByteBuffer buffer = this.buffer.duplicate();\n        buffer.position(RECORDS_OFFSET);\n        return Compression.of(compressionType()).build().wrapForInput(buffer, magic(), bufferSupplier);\n    }\n\n    private CloseableIterator<Record> compressedIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier, boolean skipKeyValue) {\n        final InputStream inputStream = recordInputStream(bufferSupplier);\n\n        if (skipKeyValue) {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readPartiallyFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        } else {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        }\n    }\n\n    private CloseableIterator<Record> uncompressedIterator() {\n        final ByteBuffer buffer = this.buffer.duplicate();\n        buffer.position(RECORDS_OFFSET);\n        return new RecordIterator() {\n            @Override\n            protected Record readNext(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) {\n                try {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(buffer, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                } catch (BufferUnderflowException e) {\n                    throw new InvalidRecordException(\"Incorrect declared batch size, premature EOF reached\");\n                }\n            }\n            @Override\n            protected boolean ensureNoneRemaining() {\n                return !buffer.hasRemaining();\n            }\n            @Override\n            public void close() {}\n        };\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Iterator<Record> iterator() {\n        if (count() == 0)\n            return Collections.emptyIterator();\n\n        if (!isCompressed())\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // for a normal iterator, we cannot ensure that the underlying compression stream is closed,\n        // so we decompress the full record set here. Use cases which call for a lower memory footprint\n        // can use `streamingIterator` at the cost of additional complexity\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iterator = compressedIterator(BufferSupplier.NO_CACHING, false)) {\n            List<Record> records = new ArrayList<>(count());\n            while (iterator.hasNext())\n                records.add(iterator.next());\n            return records.iterator();\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> skipKeyValueIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (count() == 0) {\n            return CloseableIterator.wrap(Collections.emptyIterator());\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * For uncompressed iterator, it is actually not worth skipping key / value / headers at all since\n         * its ByteBufferInputStream's skip() function is less efficient compared with just reading it actually\n         * as it will allocate new byte array.\n         */\n        if (!isCompressed())\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // we define this to be a closable iterator so that caller (i.e. the log validator) needs to close it\n        // while we can save memory footprint of not decompressing the full record set ahead of time\n        return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, true);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (isCompressed())\n            return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, false);\n        else\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setLastOffset(long offset) {\n        buffer.putLong(BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, offset - lastOffsetDelta());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n        long currentMaxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        // We don't need to recompute crc if the timestamp is not updated.\n        if (timestampType() == timestampType && currentMaxTimestamp == maxTimestamp)\n            return;\n\n        byte attributes = computeAttributes(compressionType(), timestampType, isTransactional(), isControlBatch(), hasDeleteHorizonMs());\n        buffer.putShort(ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, attributes);\n        buffer.putLong(MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, maxTimestamp);\n        long crc = computeChecksum();\n        ByteUtils.writeUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET, crc);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setPartitionLeaderEpoch(int epoch) {\n        buffer.putInt(PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, epoch);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long checksum() {\n        return ByteUtils.readUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    public boolean isValid() {\n        return sizeInBytes() >= RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD && checksum() == computeChecksum();\n    }\n\n    private long computeChecksum() {\n        return Crc32C.compute(buffer, ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, buffer.limit() - ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    private byte attributes() {\n        // note we're not using the second byte of attributes\n        return (byte) buffer.getShort(ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean equals(Object o) {\n        if (this == o)\n            return true;\n        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass())\n            return false;\n\n        DefaultRecordBatch that = (DefaultRecordBatch) o;\n        return Objects.equals(buffer, that.buffer);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int hashCode() {\n        return buffer != null ? buffer.hashCode() : 0;\n    }\n\n    private static byte computeAttributes(CompressionType type, TimestampType timestampType,\n                                          boolean isTransactional, boolean isControl, boolean isDeleteHorizonSet) {\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Timestamp type must be provided to compute attributes for message \" +\n                    \"format v2 and above\");\n\n        byte attributes = isTransactional ? TRANSACTIONAL_FLAG_MASK : 0;\n        if (isControl)\n            attributes |= CONTROL_FLAG_MASK;\n        if (type.id > 0)\n            attributes |= (byte) (COMPRESSION_CODEC_MASK & type.id);\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            attributes |= TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK;\n        if (isDeleteHorizonSet)\n            attributes |= DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK;\n        return attributes;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Writes an empty (zero-record) batch header into the given buffer at its current position.\n     * This is used during log compaction to preserve producer sequence metadata when all records\n     * in a batch have been deleted.\n     *\n     * <p>The written header occupies exactly {@link #RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD} bytes. The CRC is\n     * computed and written as part of this call.\n     *\n     * @param buffer               the destination buffer; must have at least\n     *                             {@link #RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD} bytes remaining\n     * @param magic                the record format magic byte; must be\n     *                             {@link RecordBatch#MAGIC_VALUE_V2} or higher\n     * @param producerId           the producer id to embed in the header\n     * @param producerEpoch        the producer epoch to embed in the header\n     * @param baseSequence         the base sequence number to embed in the header\n     * @param baseOffset           the base (first) offset of the original batch\n     * @param lastOffset           the last offset of the original batch\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch the leader epoch at the time the batch was written\n     * @param timestampType        the timestamp type ({@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME} or\n     *                             {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME})\n     * @param timestamp            the timestamp to record in the header\n     * @param isTransactional      whether this batch was produced as part of a transaction\n     * @param isControlRecord      whether this batch is a control batch\n     * @see #writeHeader\n     */\n    public static void writeEmptyHeader(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                        byte magic,\n                                        long producerId,\n                                        short producerEpoch,\n                                        int baseSequence,\n                                        long baseOffset,\n                                        long lastOffset,\n                                        int partitionLeaderEpoch,\n                                        TimestampType timestampType,\n                                        long timestamp,\n                                        boolean isTransactional,\n                                        boolean isControlRecord) {\n        int offsetDelta = (int) (lastOffset - baseOffset);\n        writeHeader(buffer, baseOffset, offsetDelta, DefaultRecordBatch.RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD, magic,\n                    CompressionType.NONE, timestampType, RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP, timestamp, producerId,\n                    producerEpoch, baseSequence, isTransactional, isControlRecord, false, partitionLeaderEpoch, 0);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Encodes a complete magic v2 batch header into the given buffer at its current position and\n     * advances the buffer position by {@link #RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD} bytes. The CRC-32C checksum\n     * covering all header fields from the attributes to the end of the declared batch size is\n     * computed and written inline.\n     *\n     * <p>This is a low-level method used by {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} during batch\n     * serialisation. Most callers should use {@link MemoryRecords#builder} or\n     * {@link #writeEmptyHeader} instead.\n     *\n     * @param buffer               the destination buffer; must have at least {@code sizeInBytes}\n     *                             bytes remaining from the current position\n     * @param baseOffset           the base (first) offset of the batch\n     * @param lastOffsetDelta      difference between the last and base offsets in the batch\n     * @param sizeInBytes          total serialised size of the batch in bytes, including this header\n     * @param magic                the record format magic byte; must be\n     *                             {@link RecordBatch#MAGIC_VALUE_V2} or higher\n     * @param compressionType      the compression codec used for the record data\n     * @param timestampType        the timestamp type ({@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME} or\n     *                             {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME})\n     * @param baseTimestamp        the base timestamp; used to compute per-record timestamp deltas,\n     *                             or {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP} if not applicable\n     * @param maxTimestamp         the maximum timestamp among all records in the batch\n     * @param producerId           the idempotent/transactional producer id, or\n     *                             {@link RecordBatch#NO_PRODUCER_ID}\n     * @param epoch                the producer epoch, or {@link RecordBatch#NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH}\n     * @param sequence             the base sequence number, or {@link RecordBatch#NO_SEQUENCE}\n     * @param isTransactional      whether this batch belongs to a transaction\n     * @param isControlBatch       whether this is a control batch\n     * @param isDeleteHorizonSet   whether the delete horizon flag should be set in the attributes;\n     *                             when true, {@code baseTimestamp} encodes the delete horizon time\n     * @param partitionLeaderEpoch the leader epoch at the time of writing\n     * @param numRecords           number of records contained in the batch\n     * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code magic} is below\n     *         {@link RecordBatch#CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE} or if {@code baseTimestamp} is negative and\n     *         not equal to {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP}\n     */\n    public static void writeHeader(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                   long baseOffset,\n                                   int lastOffsetDelta,\n                                   int sizeInBytes,\n                                   byte magic,\n                                   CompressionType compressionType,\n                                   TimestampType timestampType,\n                                   long baseTimestamp,\n                                   long maxTimestamp,\n                                   long producerId,\n                                   short epoch,\n                                   int sequence,\n                                   boolean isTransactional,\n                                   boolean isControlBatch,\n                                   boolean isDeleteHorizonSet,\n                                   int partitionLeaderEpoch,\n                                   int numRecords) {\n        if (magic < RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid magic value \" + magic);\n        if (baseTimestamp < 0 && baseTimestamp != NO_TIMESTAMP)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Invalid message timestamp \" + baseTimestamp);\n\n        short attributes = computeAttributes(compressionType, timestampType, isTransactional, isControlBatch, isDeleteHorizonSet);\n\n        int position = buffer.position();\n        buffer.putLong(position + BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, baseOffset);\n        buffer.putInt(position + LENGTH_OFFSET, sizeInBytes - LOG_OVERHEAD);\n        buffer.putInt(position + PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, partitionLeaderEpoch);\n        buffer.put(position + MAGIC_OFFSET, magic);\n        buffer.putShort(position + ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, attributes);\n        buffer.putLong(position + BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, baseTimestamp);\n        buffer.putLong(position + MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, maxTimestamp);\n        buffer.putInt(position + LAST_OFFSET_DELTA_OFFSET, lastOffsetDelta);\n        buffer.putLong(position + PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET, producerId);\n        buffer.putShort(position + PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET, epoch);\n        buffer.putInt(position + BASE_SEQUENCE_OFFSET, sequence);\n        buffer.putInt(position + RECORDS_COUNT_OFFSET, numRecords);\n        long crc = Crc32C.compute(buffer, ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, sizeInBytes - ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n        buffer.putInt(position + CRC_OFFSET, (int) crc);\n        buffer.position(position + RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public String toString() {\n        return \"RecordBatch(magic=\" + magic() + \", offsets=[\" + baseOffset() + \", \" + lastOffset() + \"], \" +\n                \"sequence=[\" + baseSequence() + \", \" + lastSequence() + \"], \" +\n                \"partitionLeaderEpoch=\" + partitionLeaderEpoch() + \", \" +\n                \"isTransactional=\" + isTransactional() + \", isControlBatch=\" + isControlBatch() + \", \" +\n                \"compression=\" + compressionType() + \", timestampType=\" + timestampType() + \", crc=\" + checksum() + \")\";\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Computes the serialised size in bytes of a magic v2 batch containing the given\n     * {@link Record} objects, starting at {@code baseOffset}.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This method iterates over all records in order to accumulate\n     * per-record sizes (including variable-length fields and varint-encoded deltas). It does not\n     * account for the overhead of any compression codec.\n     *\n     * @param baseOffset the base offset of the batch; used to compute per-record offset deltas\n     * @param records    the records whose encoded sizes should be summed; must not be {@code null}\n     * @return the total batch size in bytes (header plus all record bytes), or {@code 0} if\n     *         {@code records} is empty\n     */\n    public static int sizeInBytes(long baseOffset, Iterable<Record> records) {\n        Iterator<Record> iterator = records.iterator();\n        if (!iterator.hasNext())\n            return 0;\n\n        int size = RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD;\n        Long baseTimestamp = null;\n        while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n            Record record = iterator.next();\n            int offsetDelta = (int) (record.offset() - baseOffset);\n            if (baseTimestamp == null)\n                baseTimestamp = record.timestamp();\n            long timestampDelta = record.timestamp() - baseTimestamp;\n            size += DefaultRecord.sizeInBytes(offsetDelta, timestampDelta, record.key(), record.value(),\n                    record.headers());\n        }\n        return size;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Computes the serialised size in bytes of a magic v2 batch containing the given\n     * {@link SimpleRecord} objects, assuming sequential offset assignment starting at delta 0.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This method iterates over all records in order to accumulate\n     * per-record sizes.                                        List<Record> retainedRecords,\n                                                                 ByteBufferOutputStream bufferOutputStream,\n Duplicate buffer\n        // is backed by original bytes hence not the content but only the relative position and limit\n        // are changed in the duplicate buffer. Once the position and limit are set, we can call the\n        // slice method to get the sliced buffer, which is a backed by the original buffer with the\n        // position reset to 0 and limit set to the size of the slice.\n        ByteBuffer slicedBuffer = buffer.duplicate();\n        slicedBuffer.position(position);\n        slicedBuffer.limit(position + availableBytes);\n        // Reset the position to 0 so that the sliced view has a relative position.\n        slicedBuffer = slicedBuffer.slice();\n\n        return readableRecords(slicedBuffer);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Returns an {@link Iterable} over the {@link MutableRecordBatch} objects contained in this\n     * instance. The iterable is backed by a lazy {@link #batchIterator()} and can be iterated\n     * multiple times; each call to {@link Iterable#iterator()} creates a new independent iterator\n     * over the same underlying buffer.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> Batch-level metadata (offsets, timestamps, compression type) is\n     * read directly from the backing buffer without decompression. Record-level access requires\n     * explicit iteration into each batch.\n     *\n     * @return an {@link Iterable} of {@link MutableRecordBatch}; never {@code null}\n     */\n    @Override\n    public Iterable<MutableRecordBatch> batches() {\n        return batches;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public String toString() {\n        return \"MemoryRecords(size=\" + sizeInBytes() +\n                \", buffer=\" + buffer +\n                \")\";\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean equals(Object o) {\n        if (this == o)\n            return true;\n        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass())\n            return false;\n\n        MemoryRecords that = (MemoryRecords) o;\n\n        return buffer.equals(that.buffer);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int hashCode() {\n        return buffer.hashCode();\n    }\n\n    public abstract static class RecordFilter {\n        public final long currentTime;\n        public final long deleteRetentionMs;\n\n        public RecordFilter(final long currentTime, final long deleteRetentionMs) {\n            this.currentTime = currentTime;\n            this.deleteRetentionMs = deleteRetentionMs;\n        }\n\n        public static class BatchRetentionResult {\n            public final BatchRetention batchRetention;\n            public final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n            public BatchRetentionResult(final BatchRetention batchRetention,\n                                        final boolean containsMarkerForEmptyTxn) {\n                this.batchRetention = batchRetention;\n                this.containsMarkerForEmptyTxn = containsMarkerForEmptyTxn;\n            }\n        }\n\n        public enum BatchRetention {\n            DELETE, // Delete the batch without inspecting records\n            RETAIN_EMPTY, // Retain the batch even if it is empty\n            DELETE_EMPTY  // Delete the batch if it is empty\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Check whether the full batch can be discarded (i.e. whether we even need to\n         * check the records individually).\n         */\n        protected abstract BatchRetentionResult checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch batch);\n\n        /**\n         * Check whether a record should be retained in the log. Note that {@link #checkBatchRetention(RecordBatch)}\n         * is used prior to checking individual record retention. Only records from batches which were not\n         * explicitly discarded with {@link BatchRetention#DELETE} will be considered.\n         */\n        protected abstract boolean shouldRetainRecord(RecordBatch recordBatch, Record record);\n    }\n\n    public static class FilterResult {\n        private ByteBuffer outputBuffer;\n        private int messagesRead = 0;\n        // Note that `bytesRead` should contain only bytes from batches that have been processed, i.e. bytes from\n        // `messagesRead` and any discarded batches.\n        private int bytesRead = 0;\n        private int messagesRetained = 0;\n        private int bytesRetained = 0;\n        private long maxOffset = -1L;\n        private long maxTimestamp = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        private long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp = -1L;\n\n        private FilterResult(ByteBuffer outputBuffer) {\n            this.outputBuffer = outputBuffer;\n        }\n\n        private void updateRetainedBatchMetadata(MutableRecordBatch retainedBatch, int numMessagesInBatch, boolean headerOnly) {\n            int bytesRetained = headerOnly ? DefaultRecordBatch.RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD : retainedBatch.sizeInBytes();\n            updateRetainedBatchMetadata(retainedBatch.maxTimestamp(), retainedBatch.lastOffset(),\n                    retainedBatch.lastOffset(), numMessagesInBatch, bytesRetained);\n        }\n\n        private void updateRetainedBatchMetadata(long maxTimestamp, long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, long maxOffset,\n                                                 int messagesRetained, int bytesRetained) {\n            validateBatchMetadata(maxTimestamp, shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, maxOffset);\n            if (maxTimestamp > this.maxTimestamp) {\n                this.maxTimestamp = maxTimestamp;\n                this.shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp = shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp;\n            }\n            this.maxOffset = Math.max(maxOffset, this.maxOffset);\n            this.messagesRetained += messagesRetained;\n            this.bytesRetained += bytesRetained;\n        }\n\n        private void validateBatchMetadata(long maxTimestamp, long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp, long maxOffset) {\n            if (maxTimestamp != RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP && shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp < 0)\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"shallowOffset undefined for maximum timestamp \" + maxTimestamp);\n            if (maxOffset < 0)\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"maxOffset undefined\");\n        }\n\n        public ByteBuffer outputBuffer() {\n            return outputBuffer;\n        }\n\n        public int messagesRead() {\n            return messagesRead;\n        }\n\n        public int bytesRead() {\n            return bytesRead;\n        }\n\n        public int messagesRetained() {\n            return messagesRetained;\n        }\n\n        public int bytesRetained() {\n            return bytesRetained;\n        }\n\n        public long maxOffset() {\n            return maxOffset;\n        }\n\n        public long maxTimestamp() {\n            return maxTimestamp;\n        }\n\n        public long shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp() {\n            return shallowOffsetOfMaxTimestamp;\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a read-only {@link MemoryRecords} view over the given {@link ByteBuffer}. The\n     * buffer's current position is treated as the start of the first batch; the limit determines\n     * the total readable size.\n     *\n     * <p>No data is copied \u2014 the returned instance shares the underlying byte array with the\n     * supplied buffer.\n     *\n     * @param buffer the buffer containing encoded record batches; must not be {@code null}\n     * @return a {@link MemoryRecords} backed by {@code buffer}\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecords readableRecords(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        return new MemoryRecords(buffer);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for constructing a new batch using the current magic\n     * version, the given compression and timestamp type, and starting at {@code baseOffset}.\n     *\n     * @param buffer        the buffer to write the encoded batch into; must not be {@code null}\n     * @param compression   the compression codec to apply to record data\n     * @param timestampType the timestamp type ({@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME} or\n     *                      {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME})\n     * @param baseOffset    the base offset of the first record in the batch\n     * @return a new {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} ready to accept records\n     * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset) {\n        return builder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for constructing a new batch using the current magic\n     * version, the given compression and timestamp type, starting at {@code baseOffset}, and\n     * capped at {@code maxSize} bytes.\n     *\n     * <p>When the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, the log-append\n     * timestamp is set to the current wall-clock time at the moment this method is called.\n     *\n     * @param buffer        the buffer to write the encoded batch into; must not be {@code null}\n     * @param compression   the compression codec to apply to record data\n     * @param timestampType the timestamp type\n     * @param baseOffset    the base offset of the first record in the batch\n     * @param maxSize       maximum number of bytes the builder may write into {@code buffer}\n     * @return a new {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} ready to accept records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               int maxSize) {\n        long logAppendTime = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            logAppendTime = System.currentTimeMillis();\n\n        return new MemoryRecordsBuilder(buffer, RecordBatch.CURRENT_MAGIC_VALUE, compression, timestampType, baseOffset,\n            logAppendTime, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE,\n            false, false, RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH, maxSize);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} for constructing a new batch with the specified\n     * magic version, compression, timestamp type, and explicit log-append time. No idempotent or\n     * transactional producer metadata is set.\n     *\n     * @param buffer        the buffer to write the encoded batch into; must not be {@code null}\n     * @param magic         the record format magic byte\n     * @param compression   the compression codec to apply to record data\n     * @param timestampType the timestamp type\n     * @param baseOffset    the base offset of the first record in the batch\n     * @param logAppendTime the log-append timestamp to embed in the batch header;\n     *                      use {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP} if not applicable\n     * @return a new {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} ready to accept records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset,\n                                               long logAppendTime) {\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE, false,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} with the specified magic version, compression, and\n     * timestamp type. The log-append timestamp is set automatically if the timestamp type is\n     * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}. No idempotent or transactional producer metadata is\n     * set.\n     *\n     * @param buffer        the buffer to write the encoded batch into; must not be {@code null}\n     * @param magic         the record format magic byte\n     * @param compression   the compression codec to apply to record data\n     * @param timestampType the timestamp type\n     * @param baseOffset    the base offset of the first record in the batch\n     * @return a new {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} ready to accept records\n     */\n    public static MemoryRecordsBuilder builder(ByteBuffer buffer,\n                                               byte magic,\n                                               Compression compression,\n                                               TimestampType timestampType,\n                                               long baseOffset) {\n        long logAppendTime = RecordBatch.NO_TIMESTAMP;\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n            logAppendTime = System.currentTimeMillis();\n        return builder(buffer, magic, compression, timestampType, baseOffset, logAppendTime,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_ID, RecordBatch.NO_PRODUCER_EPOCH, RecordBatch.NO_SEQUENCE, false,\n                RecordBatch.NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Creates a {@link MemoryRecordsBuilder} with the specified magic version, compression,\n     * timestamp type, log-append time, and partition leader epoch. It is the fundamental unit of data transfer between producers,\n * brokers, and consumers.\n *\n * <p>The batch format has evolved over three major versions, identified by the {@link #magic()} byte:\n * <ul>\n *   <li><b>Magic v0</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V0}): Legacy format. A batch always contains exactly\n *       one record when uncompressed; multiple records are allowed only under compression.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v1</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V1}): Adds per-record timestamps. Same single-record\n *       constraint as v0 when uncompressed.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v2</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V2}) and above: Current format. Batches generally\n *       contain multiple records regardless of compression. Adds idempotent producer support\n *       (producer id, epoch, sequence numbers) and transactional semantics.</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * <p>Instances of this interface are obtained by iterating over a {@link Records} object (e.g.\n * {@link MemoryRecords} or {@code FileRecords}) via {@link Records#batches()}. They provide\n * shallow access to batch-level metadata (offsets, timestamps, producer identity, compression) as\n * well as deep access to the individual {@link Record} objects contained within.\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> Implementations of this interface are <em>not</em> thread-safe.\n * External synchronisation is required when a single batch instance is accessed concurrently from\n * multiple threads. In practice, batches are short-lived objects consumed on a single thread\n * during fetch or log-append operations.\n *\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see DefaultRecordBatch\n * @see Record\n */\npublic   */\n    int NO_PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH = -1;\n\n    /**\n     * Check whether the checksum of this batch is correct.\n     *\n     * @return true If so, false otherwise\n     */\n    boolean Reusing the\n     * {@link BufferSupplier}-supplied buffers across calls (e.g. via a thread-local pool) can\n     * significantly reduce GC pressure, especially for large batches or high-throughput consumers.\n     *\n     * @param decompressionBufferSupplier The supplier of ByteBuffer(s) used for decompression if supported.\n     *                                    For small record batches, allocating a potentially large buffer (64 KB for LZ4)\n     *                                    will dominate the cost of decompressing and iterating over the records in the\n     *                                    batch. Avoid calling this method in hot paths unless necessary.\n     *\n     * @return the offset of the record with the maximum timestamp, or {@link Optional#empty()} for\n     *         magic v0 batches or when no matching record is found\n     */\n    default Optional<Long> offsetOfMaxTimestamp() {\n        if (magic() == RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V0) return Optional.empty();\n        long maxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iter = streamingIterator(BufferSupplier.create())) {\n            while (iter.hasNext()) {\n                Record record = iter.next();\n                if (maxTimestamp == record.timestamp()) return Optional.of(record.offset());\n            }\n        }\n        return Optional.empty();\n    }\n}\n",

A batch always contains exactly\n *       one record when uncompressed; multiple records are allowed only under compression.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v1</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V1}): Adds per-record timestamps. Same single-record\n *       constraint as v0 when uncompressed.</li>\n *   <li><b>Magic v2</b> ({@link #MAGIC_VALUE_V2}) and above: Current format. Batches generally\n *       contain multiple records regardless of compression. Adds idempotent producer support\n *       (producer id, epoch, sequence numbers) and transactional semantics.</li>\n * </ul>\n *\n * <p>Instances of this interface are obtained by iterating over a {@link Records} object (e.g.\n * {@link MemoryRecords} or {@code FileRecords}) via {@link Records#batches()}.   "content": "/*\n * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\n * contributor license agreements. This class provides both read and\n * in-place-mutation access to a single batch encoded in the Kafka binary wire format. The on-wire\n * schema is:\n *\n * <pre>\n * RecordBatch =&gt;\n *   BaseOffset            =&gt; Int64\n *   Length                =&gt; Int32\n *   PartitionLeaderEpoch  =&gt; Int32\n *   Magic                 =&gt; Int8\n *   CRC                   =&gt; Uint32\n *   Attributes            =&gt; Int16\n *   LastOffsetDelta       =&gt; Int32  // also serves as LastSequenceDelta\n *   BaseTimestamp         =&gt; Int64\n *   MaxTimestamp          =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerId            =&gt; Int64\n *   ProducerEpoch         =&gt; Int16\n *   BaseSequence          =&gt; Int32\n *   RecordsCount          =&gt; Int32\n *   Records               =&gt; [Record]\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p>When compression is enabled (see attributes below), the compressed record data is serialized\n * directly following the count of the number of records.\n *\n * <p>The CRC covers the data from the attributes to the end of the batch (i.e. all the bytes that\n * follow the CRC). It is located after the magic byte, which means that clients must parse the\n * magic byte before deciding how to interpret the bytes between the batch length and the magic\n * byte. The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC computation to avoid the need\n * to recompute the CRC when this field is assigned for every batch that is received by the broker.\n * The CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used for the computation.\n *\n * <p><b>Compaction:</b> Unlike the older message formats, magic v2 and above preserves the first\n * and last offset/sequence numbers from the original batch when the log is cleaned. This is\n * required in order to be able to restore the producer's state when the log is reloaded. If we did\n * not retain the last sequence number, then following a partition leader failure, once the new\n * leader has rebuilt the producer state from the log, the next sequence expected number would no\n * longer be in sync with what was written by the client. This would cause an unexpected\n * {@code OutOfOrderSequence} error, which is typically fatal. The base sequence number must be\n * preserved for duplicate checking: the broker checks incoming Produce requests for duplicates by\n * verifying that the first and last sequence numbers of the incoming batch match the last from that\n * producer.\n *\n * <p>Note that if all of the records in a batch are removed during compaction, the broker may\n * still retain an empty batch header in order to preserve the producer sequence information as\n * described above. These empty batches are retained only until either a new sequence number is\n * written by the corresponding producer or the producerId is expired from lack of activity.\n *\n * <p>There is no similar need to preserve the timestamp from the original batch after compaction.\n * The {@code BaseTimestamp} field therefore reflects the timestamp of the first record in the\n * batch in most cases. If the batch is empty, the {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to\n * {@link RecordBatch#NO_TIMESTAMP}. If the delete horizon flag is set to 1, the\n * {@code BaseTimestamp} will be set to the time at which tombstone records and aborted transaction\n * markers in the batch should be removed.\n *\n * <p>Similarly, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field reflects the maximum timestamp of the current\n * records if the timestamp type is {@link TimestampType#CREATE_TIME}. For\n * {@link TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME}, on the other hand, the {@code MaxTimestamp} field\n * reflects the timestamp set by the broker and is preserved after compaction. Additionally, the\n * {@code MaxTimestamp} of an empty batch always retains the previous value prior to becoming empty.\n *\n * <p>The current attributes bit layout:\n * <pre>\n *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  | Unused (7-15) | Delete Horizon Flag (6) | Control (5) | Transactional (4) | Timestamp Type (3) | Compression Type (0-2) |\n *  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n * </pre>\n *\n * <p><b>Thread-safety:</b> This class is <em>not</em> thread-safe. The underlying\n * {@link ByteBuffer} is accessed without synchronisation. Concurrent reads or any combination of\n * reads and in-place mutations (e.g. {@link #setLastOffset}, {@link #setMaxTimestamp},\n * {@link #setPartitionLeaderEpoch}) from multiple threads requires external synchronisation.\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see MemoryRecordsBuilder\n */\npublic class DefaultRecordBatch extends AbstractRecordBatch implements MutableRecordBatch null}\n     * @return an {@link InputStream} over the (possibly decompressed) record bytes\n     */\n    public InputStream recordInputStream(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        final ByteBuffer private CloseableIterator<Record> compressedIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier, boolean skipKeyValue) {\n        final InputStream inputStream = recordInputStream(bufferSupplier);\n\n        if (skipKeyValue) {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readPartiallyFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        } else {\n            return new StreamRecordIterator(inputStream) {\n                @Override\n                protected Record doReadRecord(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) throws IOException {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(inputStream, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                }\n            };\n        }\n    }\n\n    private CloseableIterator<Record> uncompressedIterator() {\n        final ByteBuffer buffer = this.buffer.duplicate();\n        buffer.position(RECORDS_OFFSET);\n        return new RecordIterator() {\n            @Override\n            protected Record readNext(long baseOffset, long baseTimestamp, int baseSequence, Long logAppendTime) {\n                try {\n                    return DefaultRecord.readFrom(buffer, baseOffset, baseTimestamp, baseSequence, logAppendTime);\n                } catch (BufferUnderflowException e) {\n                    throw new InvalidRecordException(\"Incorrect declared batch size, premature EOF reached\");\n                }\n            }\n            @Override\n            protected boolean ensureNoneRemaining() {\n                return !buffer.hasRemaining();\n            }\n            @Override\n            public void close() {}\n        };\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Iterator<Record> iterator() {\n        if (count() == 0)\n            return Collections.emptyIterator();\n\n        if (!isCompressed())\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // for a normal iterator, we cannot ensure that the underlying compression stream is closed,\n        // so we decompress the full record set here. Use cases which call for a lower memory footprint\n        // can use `streamingIterator` at the cost of additional complexity\n        try (CloseableIterator<Record> iterator = compressedIterator(BufferSupplier.NO_CACHING, false)) {\n            List<Record> records = new ArrayList<>(count());\n            while (iterator.hasNext())\n                records.add(iterator.next());\n            return records.iterator();\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> skipKeyValueIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (count() == 0) {\n            return CloseableIterator.wrap(Collections.emptyIterator());\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * For uncompressed iterator, it is actually not worth skipping key / value / headers at all since\n         * its ByteBufferInputStream's skip() function is less efficient compared with just reading it actually\n         * as it will allocate new byte array.\n         */\n        if (!isCompressed())\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n\n        // we define this to be a closable iterator so that caller (i.e. the log validator) needs to close it\n        // while we can save memory footprint of not decompressing the full record set ahead of time\n        return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, true);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public CloseableIterator<Record> streamingIterator(BufferSupplier bufferSupplier) {\n        if (isCompressed())\n            return compressedIterator(bufferSupplier, false);\n        else\n            return uncompressedIterator();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setLastOffset(long offset) {\n        buffer.putLong(BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, offset - lastOffsetDelta());\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setMaxTimestamp(TimestampType timestampType, long maxTimestamp) {\n        long currentMaxTimestamp = maxTimestamp();\n        // We don't need to recompute crc if the timestamp is not updated.\n        if (timestampType() == timestampType && currentMaxTimestamp == maxTimestamp)\n            return;\n\n        byte attributes = computeAttributes(compressionType(), timestampType, isTransactional(), isControlBatch(), hasDeleteHorizonMs());\n        buffer.putShort(ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, attributes);\n        buffer.putLong(MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET, maxTimestamp);\n        long crc = computeChecksum();\n        ByteUtils.writeUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET, crc);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void setPartitionLeaderEpoch(int epoch) {\n        buffer.putInt(PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, epoch);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long checksum() {\n        return ByteUtils.readUnsignedInt(buffer, CRC_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    public boolean isValid() {\n        return sizeInBytes() >= RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD && checksum() == computeChecksum();\n    }\n\n    private long computeChecksum() {\n        return Crc32C.compute(buffer, ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET, buffer.limit() - ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    private byte attributes() {\n        // note we're not using the second byte of attributes\n        return (byte) buffer.getShort(ATTRIBUTES_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean equals(Object o) {\n        if (this == o)\n            return true;\n        if (o == null || getClass() != o.getClass())\n            return false;\n\n        DefaultRecordBatch that = (DefaultRecordBatch) o;\n        return Objects.equals(buffer, that.buffer);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public int hashCode() {\n        return buffer != null ? buffer.hashCode() : 0;\n    }\n\n    private static byte computeAttributes(CompressionType type, TimestampType timestampType,\n                                          boolean isTransactional, boolean isControl, boolean isDeleteHorizonSet) {\n        if (timestampType == TimestampType.NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Timestamp type must be provided to compute attributes for message \" +\n                    \"format v2 and above\");\n\n        byte attributes = isTransactional ? epoch,\n                                   int sequence,\n                                   boolean isTransactional,\n                                   boolean isControlBatch,\n                                   boolean isDeleteHorizonSet,\n                                   int partitionLeaderEpoch,\n                                   int numRecords) {\n        if (magic < isDeleteHorizonSet);\n\n        int position = buffer.position();\n        buffer.putLong(position + BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET, baseOffset);\n        buffer.putInt(position + LENGTH_OFFSET, sizeInBytes - LOG_OVERHEAD);\n        buffer.putInt(position + PARTITION_LEADER_EPOCH_OFFSET, partitionLeaderEpoch);\n        buffer.put(position + MAGIC_OFFSET, magic);\n        buffer.putShort(position + It does not\n     * account for the overhead of any compression codec.\n     *\n     * @param baseOffset the base offset of the batch; used to compute per-record offset deltas\n     * @param records    the records whose encoded sizes should be summed; must not be {@code null}\n     * @return the total batch size in bytes (header plus all record bytes), or {@code 0} if\n     *         {@code records} is empty\n     */\n    public static int sizeInBytes(long baseOffset, Iterable<Record> records) {\n        Iterator<Record> iterator = records.iterator();\n        if (!iterator.hasNext())\n            return 0;\n\n        int size = RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD;\n        Long baseTimestamp = null;\n        while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n            Record record = iterator.next();\n            int offsetDelta = (int) (record.offset() - baseOffset);\n            if (baseTimestamp == null)\n                baseTimestamp = record.timestamp();\n            long timestampDelta = record.timestamp() - baseTimestamp;\n            size += DefaultRecord.sizeInBytes(offsetDelta, timestampDelta, record.key(), record.value(),\n                    record.headers());\n        }\n        return size;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Computes the serialised size in bytes of a magic v2 batch containing the given\n     * {@link SimpleRecord} objects, assuming sequential offset assignment starting at delta 0.\n     *\n     * <p><b>Performance note:</b> This method iterates over all records in order to accumulate\n     * per-record sizes. This method implements the wrap-around correctly so that\n     * brokers can detect duplicate and out-of-order produce requests even across sequence-number\n     * rollovers.\n     *\n     * @param sequence  the current base sequence number; must be non-negative\n     * @param increment the value to add; must be non-negative\n     * @return the resulting sequence number after incrementing, with wrap-around applied\n     * @see #decrementSequence(int, int)\n     */\n    public static int incrementSequence(int sequence, int increment) {\n        if (sequence > Integer.MAX_VALUE - increment)\n            return increment - (Integer.MAX_VALUE - sequence) - 1;\n        return sequence + increment;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Decrements a producer sequence number by {@code decrement}, wrapping around at zero\n     * according to the Kafka sequence-number arithmetic.\n     *\n     * <p>This is the inverse of {@link #incrementSequence(int, int)}. decrementSequence(int sequence, int decrement) {\n        if (sequence < decrement)\n            return Integer.MAX_VALUE - (decrement - sequence) + 1;\n        return sequence - decrement;\n    }\n\n
